  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_6158d87e-249b-4a8e-ac49-1946bfd2fac2'
      });
    }
    
    var initializeSiwa = function() {
      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"
      loadScript(APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL, initAppleId);
    };

      initAppleId();
    } else {
      initializeSiwa();

<span id="freeTextContainer3141002041677173915">Wendy Everly is facing an impossible choice. The only way to save the Trylle from their deadliest enemy is by sacrificing herself.  If she doesn't surrender to the Vittra, her people will be thrust into a brutal war against an unbeatable foe.  But how can Wendy leave all her friends behind... even if it’s the only way to save them?<br/><br/>The stakes have never been higher, because</span>
  <span id="freeText3141002041677173915" style="display:none">Wendy Everly is facing an impossible choice. The only way to save the Trylle from their deadliest enemy is by sacrificing herself.  If she doesn't surrender to the Vittra, her people will be thrust into a brutal war against an unbeatable foe.  But how can Wendy leave all her friends behind... even if it’s the only way to save them?<br /><br />The stakes have never been higher, because her kingdom isn't the only thing she stands to lose. After falling for both Finn and Loki, she’s about to make the ultimate choice... who to love forever. One guy has finally proven to be the love of her life—and now all their lives might be coming to an end. <br /><br />Everything has been leading to this moment.  The future of her entire world rests in her hands—if she’s ready to fight for it.</span>

  <span id="freeText18338630046541764702" style="display:none">For the first time, Wendy is someone to whom you actually can give the kingdom, and it doesn't feel like a baby being handed matches and canister of petrol. <br />Tove is still is the purest soul in this wholes series, and he is just so lost in his sad life. The day after helping the survivors, I hoped that they would move in their relationship. It was something. But no... Don't get me wrong; I'm team Loki since the first book even though that he isn't there. But I really want to see something between Tove and Wendy. I ship them as BFFs. <br />When Wendy was honest with Finn, I was so happy. Shea told him the same thing I was thinking about him since the first book.<br />Really glad that there was a minimum of Matt and Rhys. <br />Anyway, the end was not written properly; there is so much to change. <div id="review_138516627" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/138516627" />
    <a title="Julie" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4090710-julie"><img alt="Julie" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1343183827p2/4090710.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/138516627?book_show_action=true">Jan 04, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Julie" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Julie" href="/user/show/4090710-julie">Julie</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/10203031-ascend">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer138516627" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6983580110536816123">With bittersweet feelings, I bring you this review of 'Ascend'. This is the last book in The Trylle Trilogy. It is just as enthralling as the first two books in the series. I am not giving spoilers here. You will want to experience the evolution with the cast of Trylle for yourself. Some may cry, some may cheer, but in my opinion, Hocking has written one of the best series in YA fantasy.<br/><br/>We left Wendy in 'Torn' engaged to her friend Tove. They really are a perfect match for each other and would b</span>
  <span id="freeText6983580110536816123" style="display:none">With bittersweet feelings, I bring you this review of 'Ascend'. This is the last book in The Trylle Trilogy. It is just as enthralling as the first two books in the series. I am not giving spoilers here. You will want to experience the evolution with the cast of Trylle for yourself. Some may cry, some may cheer, but in my opinion, Hocking has written one of the best series in YA fantasy.<br /><br />We left Wendy in 'Torn' engaged to her friend Tove. They really are a perfect match for each other and would be the strongest King and Queen Trylle has had in a very long time. The problem is that neither is in love with the other. That hasn’t changed in 'Ascend'. Their friendship and their sense of duty play a big part in the final book. Finn is still the brooding tracker, handsome as ever, and just as dedicated to his duty as Wendy and Tove are to theirs. He is also still in love with Wendy. Willa and Matt had developed a forbidden relationship and that hasn’t changed in 'Ascend'. But, will they be able to be together in the end? Ah, that is a question. Willa does a lot of growing in this book and her relationship with Matt has changed her for the better. I think you will be surprised what an eye opener Matt has become for Willa, whether they are able to stay together or not, his influence has left a lasting mark. Elora was having a rough time the last we saw her, and you will learn so much more as to why she is the cold hearted Queen we know her to be today. And Loki, the gorgeous, sarcastic, and strong Vittra Markis. No one knows if he is a good guy or a bad guy. Does he truly have feelings for Wendy or is he playing her to gain strength for the Vittra? Well, this gets answered in 'Ascend', and man oh man, it will be…interesting. He brings a spark into the mix that is fun and scary at the same time.<br /><br /> I think I liked and was annoyed by each character of this book at some point or other. I was annoyed at Tove for being so nice and responsible, but liked him because he was so nice and responsible. To me, he poses a threat to Wendy finding true love. Wendy annoyed me for putting the kingdom first over her own happiness, but then I liked her because she really grows up and takes life by the horns. Remember this, Wendy is forced to do a lot of growing up and becomes quite the woman to be reckoned with. Finn I wanted to slap because he has never fought for Wendy like I wanted, yet I liked him because when it is all said and done, he loves Wendy and does want to be with her. Elora has been so cold and distant, but she does something in 'Ascend'' that just melted my heart. And Loki. I think he has become one of my favorite characters because he’s just one you want to hate, but can’t. Regardless of his ultimate role, I appreciate his sharp wit. I laughed out loud at some of his come backs.<br /><br />I can’t give away the ending, but I can give you my opinion of a few questions I know I had before reading 'Ascend'. What happens with:<br /><br />Wendy and Finn? What should happen.<br /><br />Wendy and Tove? Not what I hoped for or expected.<br /><br />Wendy and Loki? Lots of fighting and a truce.<br /><br />Wendy and Elora? An understanding.<br /><br />Wendy and the Vittra King? An understanding.<br /><br />Wendy and Matt? He will always be her big brother.<br /><br />Another thing I can say is there is a big battle coming between the Trylle and the Vittra. This battle is key and we get to see some awesome troll powers at work. <br /><br />In the end, I agree with all the decisions each character makes. I think the evolution and growth of the characters to be unique and this book doesn’t fit some generic mold of YA fantasy. I did feel twinges of sadness at some outcomes and joyous grinning at others. Some will die, but the future of the Trylle ends up in the best hands. I will say that much. Hocking has mentioned on her blog she has toyed with the thought of a possible spin-off with some of the minor characters. So, here’s hoping we haven’t seen the last of her troll world we have grown to love. Don’t hate me for not doing spoilers. I promise this is a good read! Nothing will be left unsaid or undone. I hugged my Kindle when I was finished.<br /><br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="6983580110536816123" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer6070161874157065245">First, let me address the fact that I do love the series as a whole. Now, that being said, I found this to be the worst book in the trilogy. I read through the reviews & to be quite honest, I am totally appalled that people acually enjoy Wendy ending up with Loki. I despised him from his introduction. I was totally team Finn, but in the second book, I didn't mind if she ended up with Tove. They seemed well suited for each other. It would have been great to have them fall in love despite the marr</span>
  <span id="freeText6070161874157065245" style="display:none">First, let me address the fact that I do love the series as a whole. Now, that being said, I found this to be the worst book in the trilogy. I read through the reviews &amp; to be quite honest, I am totally appalled that people acually enjoy Wendy ending up with Loki. I despised him from his introduction. I was totally team Finn, but in the second book, I didn't mind if she ended up with Tove. They seemed well suited for each other. It would have been great to have them fall in love despite the marriage being arranged before they ever met. <br /><br />Also, the author really started to aggravate me with Tove, his character in this book became so lame. He was such a strong force in the 2nd book &amp; being Wendy's husband, he should have remained a strong main character, not so far on the back burner. And what happened to Rhys? Seriously? Just because he started dating, does not mean he would totally ignore Wendy &amp; Matt. <br /><br />uggh. im more frustrated with my disgust for loki. to me its like bella ending up with mike from the twilight saga. it doesn't make sense &amp; frustrates me to no end. *rant over* <br /><br />hopefully, i am not the only one who feels this way, but sadly, judging by the reviews left already...i probably am. </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
                  <em>
                    This review has been hidden because it contains spoilers. To view it,
                    <a href="#" onclick="Effect.toggle(&#39;reviewTextContainer144911325&#39;); return false;">click here.</a>

              <span id="reviewTextContainer144911325" class="readable"
                    style="display:none"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11831631703749756277">The third book in <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/3486415.Amanda_Hocking' title='Amanda Hocking' rel='nofollow noopener'>Amanda Hocking</a>'s Trylle trilogy was definitely a huge disappointment. After reading the first two books, I thought the story was interesting and had an intriguing storyline but overall, the entire trilogy went downhill fast. <br/><br/>In this third book, Wendy is stuck having to make decisions for the good of the kingdom or for what she really wants in life. You go through her struggles of marrying someone that she doesn't love and falling in love with the enemy. She also struggles with </span>
  <span id="freeText11831631703749756277" style="display:none">The third book in <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/3486415.Amanda_Hocking" title="Amanda Hocking" rel="nofollow noopener">Amanda Hocking</a>'s Trylle trilogy was definitely a huge disappointment. After reading the first two books, I thought the story was interesting and had an intriguing storyline but overall, the entire trilogy went downhill fast. <br /><br />In this third book, Wendy is stuck having to make decisions for the good of the kingdom or for what she really wants in life. You go through her struggles of marrying someone that she doesn't love and falling in love with the enemy. She also struggles with the growing conflict she has with her mother and the warring tensions she has with her father. <br /><br />Overall, I thought the romance in this story was definitely ridiculous. She falls in love with Loki, a Vittra royal, from the enemy kingdom who she doesn't really have feelings for in the first place. If anything, it seemed like he was a stalker and she ended up magically falling in love with him with no real development of their feelings for each other. <br /><br />Then, the entire time, I'm thinking that Wendy is in love with Finn, her tracker and that something would happen in the end with him because he is a different class and I thought Wendy would make changes to that once she is Queen but nothing happens between them. Nothing. Apparently, because Finn never fought for Wendy, she gives up on her love for him. However, in the first two books, that is all Wendy can think about is Finn and in comes Loki ... Seriously?<br /><br />And the cheating was terrible too. I couldn't get over that in the story. <br /><br />I feel like the author wrote this book about a girl who everyone falls in love with and she apparently gets everyone's cake and eats it too. Pretty much inhales it at this point. <br /><br />I did not like this book or the series. Definitely not worth anyone's time. Seriously a big fail and huge disappointment. I don't know why there are good reviews for this series because it was just terrible!! </span>

<div id="review_1416717953" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1416717953" />
    <a title="Pearl Angeli" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/31514572-pearl-angeli"><img alt="Pearl Angeli" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1588420465p2/31514572.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1416717953?book_show_action=true">Oct 14, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Pearl Angeli" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Pearl Angeli" href="/user/show/31514572-pearl-angeli">Pearl Angeli</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781447210313" href="/book/show/13383130-ascend">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31514572-pearl-angeli?shelf=2015-reads">2015-reads</a>,

<span id="freeTextContainer9589216585892112899"><blockquote>
  <i>
    <b>"Don't act on everything your heart says, but make sure you listen to it. Sometimes your heart is right."</b>
  </i>
</blockquote><br/><br/>Well, where should I start? This book... This series... *cries with happy tears<br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1424747151ra/13799241.gif' width='375' height='230' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>One of my biggest problems in reading a final book of the series is the separation anxiety that I always get. With this book, I found myself experiencing the same. It's hard to let go of a series that basically makes you feel attached to the story, the characters, and its world. <br/><br/><a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/11947829.Ascend__Trylle___3_' title='Ascend (Trylle, #3) by Amanda Hocking' rel='nofollow noopener'>Ascend</a> is another one of</span>
  <span id="freeText9589216585892112899" style="display:none"><blockquote>
  <i>
    <b>"Don't act on everything your heart says, but make sure you listen to it. Sometimes your heart is right."</b>
  </i>
</blockquote><br><br>Well, where should I start? This book... This series... *cries with happy tears<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1424747151ra/13799241.gif" width="375" height="230" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>One of my biggest problems in reading a final book of the series is the separation anxiety that I always get. With this book, I found myself experiencing the same. It's hard to let go of a series that basically makes you feel attached to the story, the characters, and its world. <br><br><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/11947829.Ascend__Trylle___3_" title="Ascend (Trylle, #3) by Amanda Hocking" rel="nofollow noopener">Ascend</a> is another one of those series-enders that basically make you feel happy and sad at the same time because of its unforgettable closure. I love how the series ended in a sweet and satisfying appeal. <br><br>So much had happened in this book. <b>Wendy</b>'s character became more developed. She became more responsible, strong, and independent. Same goes with the supporting characters -- especially <b>Loki</b>, <b>Tove</b>, <b>Finn</b>, <b>Willa</b>, and the rest of the gang.<br><br>What made this book a remarkable one was the <b>unpredictability</b>. My oh my, the romance's <i>plot twist</i> really surprised me! I was like, <i>'WOW, am I really reading what I'm reading???"</i> Because OMG, <b>MY SHIP IS SAILING SO BEAUTIFULLY and it's FOR REAL!!</b><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1399160921ra/9516624.gif" width="350" height="250" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>I practically swooned! I won't be mentioning who Wendy ended up with because it's a huge spoiler but OMG, the romance really got me in my feels!!!<br><br><blockquote>
  <i>
    <b>"I don't think I've ever really felt like I had a home before. Not until I met you."</b>
  </i>
</blockquote><br><br>What just stopped me from rating it a perfect 5 was the action scenes. As a final book of the series, the action should be intense and extremely boundless -- scenes that will wow you and give you goosebumps. But in this book, the action scenes were kind of lame and they were just basically heard from the characters and were not really seen. I was expecting really mind-blowing action scenes where supernatural powers are exhibited. There was none. :(<br><br>But all in all, this book made a really great ending, emotion-wise. I love the romance, the characters, and the satisfaction I got after reading this. <b>Trylle trilogy</b> is one of the loveliest YA fantasy series I've ever come across!<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1445568328i/16674362.jpg" width="375" height="230" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Rating: 4 Stars</span>
  <a data-text-id="9589216585892112899" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_140969237" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/140969237" />
    <a title="Seanean" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3119157-seanean"><img alt="Seanean" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1311953060p2/3119157.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/140969237?book_show_action=true">Jan 15, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Seanean" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Seanean" href="/user/show/3119157-seanean">Seanean</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/10203031-ascend">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
                  <em>
                    This review has been hidden because it contains spoilers. To view it,
                    <a href="#" onclick="Effect.toggle(&#39;reviewTextContainer140969237&#39;); return false;">click here.</a>
                  </em>
              <span id="reviewTextContainer140969237" class="readable"
                    style="display:none"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5171474850641924156"><a target='_blank' rel='noopener nofollow' href='http://librarytalker.blogspot.com/2011/01/ascend.html'>http://librarytalker.blogspot.com/201...</a><br/><br/>With Wendy's wedding approaching and war on the horizon, she must now make preparations to keep her people from dying. The choices she makes now will either guarantee the future of the Trylle or destroy them completely.<br/><br/>Final thoughts: Ugh. I am so disappointed by this book. It was an absolute mess. Hocking seems to have realized late in the game that she needed to resolve points from her first two books in this trilogy and she kind of just jams those resol</span>
  <span id="freeText5171474850641924156" style="display:none"><a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://librarytalker.blogspot.com/2011/01/ascend.html">http://librarytalker.blogspot.com/201...</a><br /><br />With Wendy's wedding approaching and war on the horizon, she must now make preparations to keep her people from dying. The choices she makes now will either guarantee the future of the Trylle or destroy them completely.<br /><br />Final thoughts: Ugh. I am so disappointed by this book. It was an absolute mess. Hocking seems to have realized late in the game that she needed to resolve points from her first two books in this trilogy and she kind of just jams those resolutions in without any honest flow. There's also a Bella Swan element here of Wendy constantly wanting to go out and save the day on her own and having the men who love her constantly tell her they won't lose her like that and "never do that again". <br /><br />Hocking also seems to have no idea about the realities of war and she even seems to forget the time period she's in. A whole city has been attacked and Wendy first sends 10 people out to go help them. Those 10 people come across the attackers in a forest and surprise them. But if everyone is driving cars and cities aren't that far away, how come the attackers stopped at all and how did the 10 scouts (who are in cars driving on roads) just happen to come across them in the forest? Later, Wendy herself goes out to the town, makes one round in the palace ballroom that's being used as a hospice, and then she goes out and cleans the town. Yup. She and the others clean. No rescuing of anyone. No burying. Cleaning.<br /><br />The romance part isn't handled well either. Wendy has three guys in her life, but the person she seemed to want the most for the first two books is just kind of there in this one and she's suddenly deeply in love with someone else. <br /><br />Another similarity to Meyer's work is the seeming need for everyone to have a happy ending. Breaking Dawn annoyed me because everyone ended up happy. Ascend is similar. All things work out for everyone good and nice. Bad guys are no longer around and/or bad. Blah blah blah. I could go on and on for days about the problems in this book.<br /><br />Hocking needs an editor desperately. Her FAQ says that she writes each book in about three weeks. It really shows in this one. Writing a book and self-publishing it doesn't mean it's necessarily worth reading and this one isn't.</span>
  <a data-text-id="5171474850641924156" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_153270780" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/153270780" />
    <a title="Reading Vacation" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5102733-reading-vacation"><img alt="Reading Vacation" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1341857406p2/5102733.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/153270780?book_show_action=true">Mar 09, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Reading Vacation" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Reading Vacation" href="/user/show/5102733-reading-vacation">Reading Vacation</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/10203031-ascend">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer153270780" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1542265070952234959">REVIEW<br/><br/>I read these three books back-to-back-to-back on my Kindle. The story had me so engaged, that I could not put it down. I was reading in the car, at school, on my bed, at the dinner table, and in the media room. You could call it an obsession.<br/><br/>In this paranormal tale, Wendy learns at the age of seventeen that she is a troll. Oh, but she isn’t just ANY troll, her past is filled with mystery, deceit, and some unexpected ancestors. Amanda Hocking carefully twisted this plot with all sorts of su</span>
  <span id="freeText1542265070952234959" style="display:none">REVIEW<br /><br />I read these three books back-to-back-to-back on my Kindle. The story had me so engaged, that I could not put it down. I was reading in the car, at school, on my bed, at the dinner table, and in the media room. You could call it an obsession.<br /><br />In this paranormal tale, Wendy learns at the age of seventeen that she is a troll. Oh, but she isn’t just ANY troll, her past is filled with mystery, deceit, and some unexpected ancestors. Amanda Hocking carefully twisted this plot with all sorts of surprises. I guarantee that you have not read a series quite like this before.<br /><br />Plain and simple – Wendy rocks! She starts out unsure and confused. I mean, who wouldn’t be questioning things if they just found out they were a troll. The beauty lies in how Wendy grows and changes. As her confidence grows, she becomes the girl (err troll) she was always meant to be.<br /><br />Let’s talk romance. Wendy has more boy trolls after her than she keep track of. They are all nice in their own way, but they each have their unique traits. Finn is protective. Loki is a flirt. Tove is like a brother. I loved them all.<br /><br />If you are looking for a battle, you have come to the right place. Amanda Hocking has written some of the most epic battle scenes ever. Sure these scenes are filled with the physical battle, but they also contain the emotions behind the fight. They were so real that I could FEEL them.<br /><br />This series about trolls surprised and entertained me. I will definitely be looking for more Amanda Hocking books to read.<br /><br />RATING<br /><br />5 Loved<br /><br />COVER COMMENTS<br /><br />I like how the covers are so similar and work together to tell the story. I also love the turquoise and black because it has a mysterious feel to it.</span>
  <a data-text-id="1542265070952234959" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_138702050" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/138702050" />
    <a title="Kristi" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4641458-kristi"><img alt="Kristi" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1360769675p2/4641458.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/138702050?book_show_action=true">Jan 05, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kristi" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kristi" href="/user/show/4641458-kristi">Kristi</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/10203031-ascend">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4641458-kristi?shelf=nook-lendable">nook-lendable</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4641458-kristi?shelf=ya">ya</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
                  <em>
                    This review has been hidden because it contains spoilers. To view it,
                    <a href="#" onclick="Effect.toggle(&#39;reviewTextContainer138702050&#39;); return false;">click here.</a>
                  </em>
              <span id="reviewTextContainer138702050" class="readable"
                    style="display:none"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10586047752061394443">One thing I truly appreciate about the author's writing is that she doesn't draw out her books with endless filler-words. I never find myself wanting to skip past parts in boredom of endless elaboration of feelings or a situation. Her writing always seems to flow at a nice pace, keeping the reader's interest throughout the entire book. <br/><br/>As for Ascend, I felt it was the perfect ending to a wonderful trilogy! <br/><br/>In this final book, Wendy finally takes over the Trylle kingdom, after her mother passes. </span>
  <span id="freeText10586047752061394443" style="display:none">One thing I truly appreciate about the author's writing is that she doesn't draw out her books with endless filler-words. I never find myself wanting to skip past parts in boredom of endless elaboration of feelings or a situation. Her writing always seems to flow at a nice pace, keeping the reader's interest throughout the entire book. <br /><br />As for Ascend, I felt it was the perfect ending to a wonderful trilogy! <br /><br />In this final book, Wendy finally takes over the Trylle kingdom, after her mother passes. Before Elora passed, I was pleased to see that Wendy and Elora shared some tender and heartfelt moments together. Elora had, for the most part, come across cold and never truly expressed love towards her daughter, Wendy. After her passing, Wendy was surprised to discover that Elora had painted numerous paintings throughout her childhood, confirming the motherly love that Elora held for her. -Especially considering that Elora sacrificed a portion of her longevity, so to speak, with each painting she did. <br /><br />The much-talked about love between Wendy/Finn or Wendy/Loki was a complete surprise to me. At first, I thought I wanted to see Wendy and Finn together, after their brief almost-happened love scene. When Wendy abruptly called it quits before they went too far, I was really disappointed, and didn't understand why Wendy would give up the opportunity to *finally* be with Finn. But as the story progressed, I realized what Ms. Hocking had in mind :) and my opinion completely changed. Wendy and Finn shared an emotional final "break-up" of sorts, in which she tells Finn why she moved forward with Loki, and gave up on the hope of a Wendy+Finn future. Finn never fought for her, to be with her, or just not enough. He was too driven to abide by the rules and with making her Queen, and that always seemed to get in the way of any future they would have had together. Loki, on the other hand, had gone through hell and back, essentially, for Wendy. As the story progresses with more Wendy/Loki moments, I had no disappointment what so ever about the final love outcome. They truly do seem perfect together, and though it was sad to see both Wendy and Finn have a little heartbreak, it was worth it in the end to see the final outcome. <br /><br />The ending of this book was perfect, and I would not change a single thing! Wendy's tyrant of a father is put to rest, thanks to Wendy, for the majority, and both Kingdoms are finally at peace with one another. The Epilogue, especially, was just absolutely amazing. It ended so well that readers won't be left sad at the end of this trilogy, but rather happy with how things are left. It was everything I was hoping, and more! <br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="10586047752061394443" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer14009719362238852840"><blockquote>
  <b>⋰⋱⋰⋱⋰⋱*Glad I'm done with the re-read*⋰⋱⋰⋱⋰⋱</b>
  <br/>
  <i>This review is purely for me and might contain spoilers and facts from the book to keep myself in the known at all time. It's also long and somewhat detailed.</i>
</blockquote><br/><b>
  <u>Second re-read: 04.06.2018</u>
</b><br/>We're back with the last book in the trilogy of <b>Wendy Luella Everly</b> (17, turns 18 in the beginning of the book). She is marrying Tove Kroner in order to save the Trylle from their deadliest enemy; the Vittra. She's not in love with him - nor is he in love wi</span>
  <span id="freeText14009719362238852840" style="display:none"><blockquote>
  <b>⋰⋱⋰⋱⋰⋱*Glad I'm done with the re-read*⋰⋱⋰⋱⋰⋱</b>
  <br>
  <i>This review is purely for me and might contain spoilers and facts from the book to keep myself in the known at all time. It's also long and somewhat detailed.</i>
</blockquote><br><b>
  <u>Second re-read: 04.06.2018</u>
</b><br>We're back with the last book in the trilogy of <b>Wendy Luella Everly</b> (17, turns 18 in the beginning of the book). She is marrying Tove Kroner in order to save the Trylle from their deadliest enemy; the Vittra. She's not in love with him - nor is he in love with her - but they respect and like each other. Wendy's heart is also breaking because she's in love with two men; who to choose? Who is right for her? Does it matter? Can she even survive the war to come? <b>Overall, the book is better than the first two</b>. Wendy has grown; she's no longer so naive, weak, dumb and annoying. So there's that. The book isn't great, but it's not a horror. Also, am I the only one in the need of Tove's story?<br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“It was worth it,” Loki said suddenly.<br>“What was?” I turned back to him.<br>“Everything I went through,” he said. “For you. It was worth it.”</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br><b><u>Other characters</u>:</b><br><i>I've put these in a spoilers tag simply because it's a long list; contains spoilers.</i><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[<br>↦ <b>Finn Holmes</b> (20), a Trylle and a tracker; it’s his job. He find the changelings and bring them back. He also acts as a guard. He and his father is apparently the best.<br>↦ <b>Matthew ‘Matt’ Everly</b> (24?), Wendy's ‘host’ brother. <b>Maggie ‘Mags’</b>, their aunt on the father side and Wendy's legal guardian. <b>Kimberly ‘Kim’ Everly</b>, their mom. Willa, as a Marksinna, dating Matt, a human is not allowed and if anybody found out, she’d be banished. She wasn’t even supposed to date him, let alone marry him.<br>↦ <b>Elora Dahl</b> (39, but looks in her fifties), Wendy's real mother. She the Queen, Wendy is the Princess. She are her only child, the last of her legacy. She will one day be Queen of Trylle. Elora has precognition: she can tell the future, but only by painting it. All she knows is what she paints, she doesn’t see anything. She picks up the brush, and it just. . . comes out. She has no control over what she sees. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Dies in this book. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br>↦ <b>Rhys Dahl</b>, a mänsklig ‘mänks’. The literal translation for mänsklig is ‘human’. Rhys is human. He were switched at birth because of a changeling; Wendy. Meaning that when she took the place of another baby, that baby had to go somewhere else. Meaning Rhys is Michael, Matt's real brother.<br>↦ <b>Willa Strom</b> (21), a Trylle. Finn had been a tracker for Willa, so he knew her and her father, <b>Garrett Stroms</b> (in his mid-forties), quite well. Garrett’s wife - Willa’s mother - had died some years earlier. The Stroms are very good friends of Elora. Willa can controlled the wind and her official title is Marksinna. Her dad is a Markis, which is just a male Marksinna.<br>↦ <b>Rhiannon</b>, a mänsklig ‘mänks’. Rhiannon is Willa’s mänsklig. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Starts dating Rhys. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br>↦ <b>Aurora Kroner</b>, Trylle and a Marksinn, her husband, <b>Noah Kroner</b> and their son, <b>Tove Kroner</b> (19). The Kroners are very important people. They affect the future. Tove is a psychic. He can sense things. And he can move things with his mind. But he can’t read your thoughts. He can see auras, though. Colors. He is particularly sensitive to emotion. And when he move things, it helps focus him. He’s like the highest Markis in the world, which is weird. The Marksinna are usually the ones with all the abilities. Guys can do some things, but they pale in comparison to what women can do, yet Tove has more ability than anybody else. Aurora’s a healer. She can touch you and fix you. That’s her ability. There are maybe six or seven other families in Förening alone with the same title. The Kroners were next in line for the crown if Wendy didn’t come back. They’re real powerful. Tove is gay.<br>↦ <b>Oren</b>, the Vittra King. <b>Sara Elsing</b>, his queen and a healer. The Vittra palace in Ondarike: the Vittra capital. Oren ages, but at a much slower rate, and he heals very quickly. It’s hard for him to be hurt. He’s one of the last pure-blooded Vittra to be born. He is nearly a hundred years old. We find out that Oren is Wendy's father.<br>↦ <b>Jen</b> and <b>Kyra</b>, Vittra trackers. Jen is really in for hurting Wendy every time they meet.<br>↦ <b>Duncan Janssen</b> (27), a Trylle tracker. Wendy’s bodyguard/shadow and one of her closest friends. Though clumsy and small, he is smarter than most people give him credit for.<br>↦ <b>Annali Holmes</b>, lowly servant of the Queen and Finn’s mother; she hates the Queen and the Princess. <b>Ember</b> (12), Finn's sister. <b>Thomas</b>, his father; the head guard in charge of security and all the trackers.<br>↦ <b>Markis Bain</b>, was in charge of changeling placement. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Ends up with Tove. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br>↦ <b>Loki Staad</b> (23), a Markis. He’s the highest Vittra royal after the King. His shaggy hair was surprisingly light for a Vittra, almost blond. Sara, the Queen, was once Loki's betrothed; an arranged marriage—until Oren decided he wanted her to be his bride. A Markis like Loki is awfully strong. Like Wendy, he is half Vittra and half Trylle. Loki has the ability to render people unconscious. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Ends up married to Wendy and they get a little boy called Oliver. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br>↦ <b>Kenna Tomas</b>, and with her parents dead, she's now the Marksinna of Oslinna.<br>↦ <b>Mia</b>, from a tracker family. <b>Hanna</b>, her daughter. Hanna's father died trying to protect them in the attack of Oslinna by the Vittra (the hobgoblins) <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Ends up with Finn. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>.<br>↦ <b>Laris</b>, a Marksinna who doesn't like Wendy. She was one of the most influential people in Förening.  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“This really is for the best,” I said. “Me and you never would’ve worked out anyway. You need someone that you can protect and shelter. And I need someone to push me to take risks, so I can pull this kingdom forward.”<br>“There is more truth in that than I’m ready to admit,” he agreed.<br>I swallowed, realizing something I’d never realized before. “I never could’ve really made you happy. I would’ve fought you at everything, frustrated by your attempts to keep me safe and hold me back. We would’ve made each other miserable.”</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br><b><u>Quick basic facts</u>:</b><br><b>Genre</b>: - (Young Adult) Paranormal/Fantasy Romance.<br><b>Series</b>: - Series, Book Three.<br><b>Love triangle?</b> - <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Not really, the choice is clear. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br><b>Cheating?</b> - <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Wendy has sex with Loki while married to Tove. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br><b>HEA?</b> - <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Yes. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br><b>Favorite character?</b> - Tove Kroner.<br><b>Would I read more by this author/or of series?</b> - Already have.<br><b>Would I recommend this book/series?</b> - Probably not. But yes, if you like YA, I guess.<br><b>Will I read this again in the future?</b> - No. <br><b>New Rating</b> - 2.5 stars.<br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1445268775i/16623124.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><b>
  <u>Re-read: 30.03.15</u>

  <u>First read: 01.01.12</u>

<div id="review_546729263" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/546729263" />
    <a title="Mizuki" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/16842102-mizuki"><img alt="Mizuki" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1368277474p2/16842102.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/546729263?book_show_action=true">Feb 26, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Mizuki" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Mizuki" href="/user/show/16842102-mizuki">Mizuki</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16842102-mizuki?shelf=young-adult-books">young-adult-books</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16842102-mizuki?shelf=disappointment">disappointment</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16842102-mizuki?shelf=supernatural-stuff">supernatural-stuff</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16842102-mizuki?shelf=i-hate-love-triangle">i-hate-love-triangle</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer546729263" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13944964039940368678">Extra Link: Amazing article by MakingFunOfStuff: <a href='http://www.deviantart.com/art/How-to-Judge-a-Book-by-its-Cover-437055930' rel='nofollow noopener'>How to Judge a Book by its Cover</a><br/><br/>What should I say concerning the last book of Miss Hocking's Trylle trilogy? Simply put, the whole thing is one hell of silly wish-fulfilling make-believe, with zero realism in the world-building, characters, setting and plot. <br/><br/>Our first and foremost problem begins with Wendy, the 'heroine' of the trilogy. In Ascend, Wendy suddenly becomes capable-leader's-material, who can keep the nobles at check? Sorry, I just can</span>
  <span id="freeText13944964039940368678" style="display:none">Extra Link: Amazing article by MakingFunOfStuff: <a href="http://www.deviantart.com/art/How-to-Judge-a-Book-by-its-Cover-437055930" rel="nofollow noopener">How to Judge a Book by its Cover</a><br /><br />What should I say concerning the last book of Miss Hocking's Trylle trilogy? Simply put, the whole thing is one hell of silly wish-fulfilling make-believe, with zero realism in the world-building, characters, setting and plot. <br /><br />Our first and foremost problem begins with Wendy, the 'heroine' of the trilogy. In Ascend, Wendy suddenly becomes capable-leader's-material, who can keep the nobles at check? Sorry, I just can't believe it. To the end of book 2, Torn; Wendy remained a whinny, immature girl and the author had offered us NOTHING to support Wendy's transition to her more mature self.<br /><br />Another character just as unbelievable as Wendy is Oren, King of Vittra and the arch villain in the story. The problem being, we barely ever have the chance to see Oren do bad things throughout the three books. For most of the time we basically only have Loki's words to proof Oren is bad, and Sara's fear to hint at how violent Oren is. But for most of the time, Oren doesn't look like a smart-enough villain to me. Towns were attacked, people were killed under his order, but none of these attacks seem to be beneficent to him in any sense. Plus, how Oren is finally defeated is purely laughable.<br /><br />How about the supporting characters? Oh, they all got shove into the background, whatever potential they had in the previous book never get developed into anything deeper.<br /><br />Okay, maybe the author wants to focus on Wendy, Finn and Loki, but if it were the case their love triangle is as badly written as the one among Bella, Edward and Jacob from Twilight. <br /><br />Aside from flat, underdeveloped characters, the world building is as shrubby as what the first two books had offered. When another Trylle's town is under Oren's attack, we are informed that all of the Trylle's towns manage to fly under humans' radar because they all locate in very remote areas. WHAT THE HELL? Are we supposed to believe in the age of internet, Google Maps and GPS, the humans and even the USA government itself are all so stupid that they are not aware of the existence of a handful of...towns?<br /><br />*plot spoiler warning*<br /><br />First, I admit I am glad that Wendy doesn't keep Finn nor Tove in the end, she doesn't deserve them anyway! I am just equally glad that Finn and Tove find happiness with someone else at the end of the book, even thought their new found happiness looks like some very clumsy attempt to please the readers.<br /><br />I also don't have problem with Wendy and Finn NOT being together, therefore I don't mind her hooking up with someone else. But the real problem with Wendy's shifting her 'love' to Loki is, I don't believe there's any meaningful, mature love between them for a *second*. <br /><br />I mean, the two barely know one another well at the first place. Plus, what's there in Wendy for Loki (or even Finn for the same matter) to fall in love with anyway? The author tells us Loki falls for Wendy because she is kind to him and she tries to protect him. Then how about Sara? Hasn't she always been kind to him and tried to protect him for all these years!? I understand how you can be grateful to someone who's kind to you, but it would take a lot more for gratefulness to develop into long-lasting love!<br /><br />Last but not least, the love scene between Wendy and Loki also made me feel damn awkward. The whole thing just takes place all of a sudden and it's quite meaningless. <br /><br />We are told that there will be a massive war between Trylle and Vittra through out two books, but when the battle finally arrives, most of the Trylle vs Vittra battle is done *off screen*, and I can't accept Wendy somehow also manages to defeat Oren, single-handed.<br /><br />*end of spoiler*<br /><br />The Final Words: <br />The whole book reads like it was written by a freaking 10 years old girl while she was playing princess-game with her freaking barbie dolls. It had been so long since the last time I encountered a YA book as poorly written and.......empty as this. But now I can confidently tell you Trylle trilogy by Amanda Hocking, is as bad and silly a series as Twilight series. Yes, they are pretty much at the same level, and this fact alone speaks volumes of what you should expect if you ever decided to read it.</span>
  <a data-text-id="13944964039940368678" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_303509944" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/303509944" />
    <a title="Giselle" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4800103-giselle"><img alt="Giselle" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1310159877p2/4800103.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/303509944?book_show_action=true">Mar 30, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Giselle" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Giselle" href="/user/show/4800103-giselle">Giselle</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4800103-giselle?shelf=arc">arc</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4800103-giselle?shelf=own">own</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer303509944" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer934107663946429610">This is it. The queen is dying. The king wants her kingdom. He will do anything to get it. Only Wendy stands in the way.<br/><br/>The final book in the Trylle Trilogy has great character development and an excellent romance. I was, however, a bit underwhelmed by the ending. We'll get to that. First, the characters. Wendy can be a bit dramatic. She will jump to decisions in a heartbeat and that kind of annoyed me at first. It's like she doesn't stop to think before she acts. I guess I should be used to her</span>
  <span id="freeText934107663946429610" style="display:none">This is it. The queen is dying. The king wants her kingdom. He will do anything to get it. Only Wendy stands in the way.<br /><br />The final book in the Trylle Trilogy has great character development and an excellent romance. I was, however, a bit underwhelmed by the ending. We'll get to that. First, the characters. Wendy can be a bit dramatic. She will jump to decisions in a heartbeat and that kind of annoyed me at first. It's like she doesn't stop to think before she acts. I guess I should be used to her by now but it irritated me more in this one. I think she may have been a bit too confident by her almost-queen status. But since she is almost the queen, she shouldn't make rash decisions. She seemed to do as she pleased without listening to advice thrown at her. So I did get a bit frustrated with her decisions. However, she still has her awesome sense of humor that had me giggling a few times. Next to her, we have the whole gang of side characters that I grew to admire from the first book. I loved Tove especially in this one, but we didn't delve much deeper into any of them except for Loki. <br /><br />Loki is the character I was the most fond of. He is an absolutely great addition to the series. Mysterious and sincere - he's a really strong character with a lot of heart. The romance he shares with Wendy is intense and honest. It's not only Loki that's been grasping at Wendy's heart, though. Finn has never left it, but she's trying to move on. I actually quite enjoyed the way the love triangle played out in this series. It didn't turn out the way I thought it would, and that was a pleasant surprise. It made it much less cliché with real emotional consequences. <br /><br />This series as a whole is not incredibly action packed. It's more about the characters and the ominous upcoming battle. This battle that finally arrives, to me, was a bit underwhelming. Having waited 2 previous books for this epic showdown, then getting it over with without much effort, not to mention a bit too perfectly, felt anticlimactic. It's very much the happily ever after ending. It wasn't bad, but I expected more emotion, more negative repercussions I guess; giving it more weight to make it memorable. Maybe I'm just a masochist. *shrugs* Regardless, I wouldn't say I was disappointed with the ending, I just wasn't wowed by it. <br /><br />This whole series is definitely fun. I loved learning about the complex world of Trylle and Vittra. It's highly original. I also had a great time getting to know the numerous characters inside it. It reads a lot like a mild fantasy novel that I'd recommend for paranormal fans who are looking for something different and creative. <br /><br />--<br />For more of my reviews, visit my blog at <a href="http://www.xpressoreads.com" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <b>Xpresso Reads</b>
</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="934107663946429610" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_150448559" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">

    <a title="Kandi" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1568021-kandi"><img alt="Kandi" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1252860143p2/1568021.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/150448559?book_show_action=true">Feb 24, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kandi" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kandi" href="/user/show/1568021-kandi">Kandi</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/10203031-ascend">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer150448559" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12443167106789064140">I went on a reading binge and read all three books in the trilogy in a 9 hour period on Saturday. They were simple reads but still had a fun story that left you wanting to know more. I decided to combine my review in one place since they all did seem to blur together because I read it as one long story instead of three separate books. First, this is a new world that I loved reading about. Something different from the standard mythical creatures that are so big right now. The person she ends up w</span>
  <span id="freeText12443167106789064140" style="display:none">I went on a reading binge and read all three books in the trilogy in a 9 hour period on Saturday. They were simple reads but still had a fun story that left you wanting to know more. I decided to combine my review in one place since they all did seem to blur together because I read it as one long story instead of three separate books. First, this is a new world that I loved reading about. Something different from the standard mythical creatures that are so big right now. The person she ends up with at the end surprised me. I don't know if it's because I read them all so quickly that I didn't see it coming, but I felt that the relationship wasn't built up enough and it seemed to catch me off guard. Also, I know that her character grew up quite a bit, and I can say I did see the progression, but I still found myself doubting her at times and not quite believing she was capable of doing what she set out to do. Wasn't in love with the Queen at first, but wow I felt for her by the third story and I couldn't believe what she went through and how hard her life was. Learning about all the sacrifices she had to make was incredible and it made me sad that Wendy didn't have more time to spend with her. I heard there will be a spin off series and I'd love to read more about this world and the other characters in this trilogy.</span>
  <a data-text-id="12443167106789064140" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_1233207691" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1233207691" />
    <a title="Cait (Caitsbooks)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/26144369-cait-caitsbooks"><img alt="Cait (Caitsbooks)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1595536856p2/26144369.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">

<div id="review_146257668" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/146257668" />
    <a title="Anita" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3202140-anita"><img alt="Anita" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1450783154p2/3202140.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/146257668?book_show_action=true">Feb 06, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Anita" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Anita" href="/user/show/3202140-anita">Anita</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/10203031-ascend">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3202140-anita?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3202140-anita?shelf=romance">romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3202140-anita?shelf=paranormal">paranormal</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3202140-anita?shelf=trolls">trolls</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
                  <em>
                    This review has been hidden because it contains spoilers. To view it,
                    <a href="#" onclick="Effect.toggle(&#39;reviewTextContainer146257668&#39;); return false;">click here.</a>
                  </em>
              <span id="reviewTextContainer146257668" class="readable"
                    style="display:none"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4124728961229687979"><b>Summary</b><br/>I read this trilogy back-to-back, so instead of three books I feel like I've read on big book.<br/><br/>In <i>Switched</i> Wendy is just starting out at another new school. She has a way of getting into trouble with students and teachers. Mostly she just doesn't fit in at all. Her mother is in a mental institute for trying to kill her when she was six years old, claiming that she wasn't her daughter - but that she was some kind of monster. Apparently, her mother wasn't too far off from the truth. At her n</span>
  <span id="freeText4124728961229687979" style="display:none"><b>Summary</b><br />I read this trilogy back-to-back, so instead of three books I feel like I've read on big book.<br /><br />In <i>Switched</i> Wendy is just starting out at another new school. She has a way of getting into trouble with students and teachers. Mostly she just doesn't fit in at all. Her mother is in a mental institute for trying to kill her when she was six years old, claiming that she wasn't her daughter - but that she was some kind of monster. Apparently, her mother wasn't too far off from the truth. At her new school, Wendy meets Finn, who introduces her and walks her through her new life as a Trylle (Troll in english). Wendy was a changling, and it is time for her to come home. But it gets even better (and what could be better than dark, handsome Finn as your guide?), Wendy isn't just any Trylle, she's the princess. <br /><br />In <i>Torn</i> it's time for Wendy to accept her role as princess and trying to behave like one, especially after she's been kidnapped for a second time. This time by her father. After a dramatic rescue, Wendy is stepping up to her duties - and doing whatever she can to do what is best for her (future) kingdom.<br /><br /> is Wendy's true thrust into power. She is married to a great friend who will walk next to her and help her lead her kingdom into victory and into change. But how does one kill an immortal king?<br /><br /><b>Review</b><br />I read all three of these books over a sick weekend, when I was stuck mostly in bed. This is not to speak bad of the trilogy, the thing is, I actually probably stayed in bed even more <i>because</i> of the books. The trilogy was very well written. Wendy is a great main character, a strong person who grows from a defiant teenager into a true leader determined to do some good. I was really impressed with the story because there were many times I was thinking that Amanda Hocking was going to go in one direction with the story - and ended not taking that route at all. The only plot point that I got right (and was happy about) was her marriage to Tove. <br /><br />So what I wasn't happy about (and this is SPOILER - so please discontinue here if you wan to read)<br /><br /><br /><br />I wanted Finn! I completely, COMPLETELY understand why Wendy chose not to go with him. He didn't fight, he didn't stand up for her. He was sucked into society. I got it. But Amanda, why did you have to write it that way?? They shared some amazing, steamy moments. Much, much better than any moment with Loki in my opinion. I understand why Loki ended up being the better fit. But STILL. Ugh.<br /><br />Oh, and this is how much I didn't care for Loki. I didn't trust him. I wanted him to betray her, so she'd go back to Finn. I also wanted Tove to step up and give her a strange fit of passion and the happy ever after in that direction. I never had eyes for Loki. But I'm not the author. And I do understand why the book went the direction it did. (I keep saying that. I want to impress that this was a trilogy worth the read though!!)</span>
  <a data-text-id="4124728961229687979" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_1064455532" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1064455532" />
    <a title="Alyssa" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/8472395-alyssa"><img alt="Alyssa" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1500935920p2/8472395.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1064455532?book_show_action=true">Sep 25, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Alyssa" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Alyssa" href="/user/show/8472395-alyssa">Alyssa</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1064455532" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1982438339924340081">***<a href='http://eaterofbooks.blogspot.com/2014/09/review-ascend-by-amanda-hocking.html' rel='nofollow noopener'>Review posted on The Eater of Books! blog</a>***<br/><br/>Ascend by Amanda Hocking<br/>Book Three of the Trylle series<br/>Publisher: St. Martin's Griffin<br/>Publication Date: April 24, 2012<br/>Rating: 4 stars<br/>Source: Review copy sent by the publisher<br/><br/>Summary (from Goodreads):<br/><br/>Wendy Everly is facing an impossible choice. The only way to save the Trylle from their deadliest enemy is by sacrificing herself. If she doesn’t surrender to the Vittra, her people will be thrust into a brutal war against an unbeatable foe. But how can </span>
  <span id="freeText1982438339924340081" style="display:none">***<a href="http://eaterofbooks.blogspot.com/2014/09/review-ascend-by-amanda-hocking.html" rel="nofollow noopener">Review posted on The Eater of Books! blog</a>***<br /><br />Ascend by Amanda Hocking<br />Book Three of the Trylle series<br />Publisher: St. Martin's Griffin<br />Publication Date: April 24, 2012<br />Rating: 4 stars<br />Source: Review copy sent by the publisher<br /><br />Summary (from Goodreads):<br /><br />Wendy Everly is facing an impossible choice. The only way to save the Trylle from their deadliest enemy is by sacrificing herself. If she doesn’t surrender to the Vittra, her people will be thrust into a brutal war against an unbeatable foe. But how can Wendy leave all her friends behind…even if it’s the only way to save them?<br /><br />The stakes have never been higher, because her kingdom isn’t the only thing she stands to lose. After falling for both Finn and Loki, she’s about to make the ultimate choice…who to love forever. One guy has finally proven to be the love of her life—and now all their lives might be coming to an end. <br /><br />Everything has been leading to this moment. The future of her entire world rests in her hands—if she’s ready to fight for it.<br /><br />What I Liked:<br /><br />Wowie, what an ending! What a conclusion novel! I have to admit, I'm really pleased with this series. Maybe because I binge-read the series and didn't have time to agonize over cliffhangers or the romance, maybe because I liked this series on the surface and didn't get heavily invested... but I really enjoyed this series!<br /><br />In this final novel of the Trylle trilogy, Wendy gets married. And eventually, has a coronation. Wendy has a lot of growing up to do, because a wedding, and a coronation, are no joke. She must find a way to stop her cruel father from harming her Trylle power, but she also figure out how to reconcile her feelings for Loki, when she is married to Tove. As the summary states, everything has been leading to this moment. <br /><br />I feel like this book was short. I think it was about the same length as the previous books, but it went by very quickly. Not very much happened in terms of large events, except for the few big ones (the wedding, the coronation, the attack on the Vittra. The plot isn't super intricate or twisty - it's very straightforward and predictable, but that didn't stop me from enjoying the book.<br /><br />We don't really figure out how everything is going to work out with Wendy's father until the very end. It seems like Wendy searches for a way to defeat him for the entire book, but doesn't have an aha moment until the climax of the novel. Which is fine, because readers are left wondering what will happen.<br /><br />The romance. Oh, my heart. The romance is perfect, in my opinion. Lots of things happen, like a stolen kiss, a marriage, an tryst, in that other. But OMG, you really have to read this book to understand. I love that one scene in the book, that one night. It is so spontaneous and Wendy doesn't think at all (or maybe she really does, maybe she had it all figured out) but it is perfect. I had a good feeling about the romance from the beginning. <br /><br />I found the vacillating romance kind of nice, actually. It wasn't vacillating, really, because from the beginning to the end, it's obvious which guy has held Wendy's attention, from fleeting friendship to love. It's obvious which relationship was an obsession (shiny new guy syndrome), which one was a safe relationship, and which one was a true, deep, meaningful relationship. In my opinion.<br /><br />Wendy is an interesting character. She acts like a child sometimes, she acts very grown and mature at other times, but honestly, I feel like she's a person that every girl can relate to, on some level? I think I really understood her, when it came to the sense of duty. For sure.<br /><br />The ending is a bit cookie-cutter perfect, and everything works out so nicely. Honestly, that's fine with me, since I wasn't out to love this series or make it my next favorite thing. I would have liked to see more depth in the series plot, this book's plot, and the ending of this book in general, but that's okay. It's really fun to read these books.<br /><br />What I Did Not Like:<br /><br />Something that bothered me was how quickly Wendy let go of her human life? Like, she barely ever thought about the life she spent seventeen years living... that struck me as odd. There are many materialistic things that I know teenagers of today's world would not want to give up, no matter how badly they fit in (or did NOT fit in). <br /><br />And I already mentioned this above, but I would have liked to see more depth in this book, and series in general. It felt very formulaic, in terms of the series plot. Become a princess, save your kingdom, kill the tyrant. Nothing more was at stake, nothing more to be done. A little cliche, I'm afraid!<br /><br />Would I Recommend It:<br /><br />Well, in general, I like this series, so I'd say that if you have this series, or any of the three books in this series, definitely give the series a shot! The series could use some depth, but it's a nice series to binge-read. And of course, if you've read books one and two, definitely read this book! Don't be left hanging!<br /><br />Rating:<br /><br />4 stars. An excellent ending to an interesting series! I think I'm ready to read Frostfire now!</span>
  <a data-text-id="1982438339924340081" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1532113407" class="readable"

<span id="freeTextContainer15592095073418752974">A lovely end to this cute series. The first time I read it, I wanted Finn and Wendy to end up together, but this time, I totally get the direction Ms Hocking went with. While Finn and Wendy had passion, duty continually got in the way of their happily ever after and after three books of this, it gets a little sickening. Loki was a wonderful character who is actually a perfect fit for Wendy and is just who she needs to help her rule her kingdom.<br/><br/>I love how Wendy grew throughout the series, too. Sh</span>
  <span id="freeText15592095073418752974" style="display:none">A lovely end to this cute series. The first time I read it, I wanted Finn and Wendy to end up together, but this time, I totally get the direction Ms Hocking went with. While Finn and Wendy had passion, duty continually got in the way of their happily ever after and after three books of this, it gets a little sickening. Loki was a wonderful character who is actually a perfect fit for Wendy and is just who she needs to help her rule her kingdom.<br /><br />I love how Wendy grew throughout the series, too. She starts off so unsure and confused; fighting every change happening in her life and yelling at everyone. It got a little annoying, and yet I still got it. But by this book, Wendy understands the role she plays and what she has to do for the good of her people, whether or not it’s good for her. She becomes the Queen she was always meant to be.<br /><br />This entire series was definitely fun and entertaining. The world is incredibly original and I love how the characters grow throughout the series. I’d recommend it to those who are looking for something enjoyable and creative.</span>
  <a data-text-id="15592095073418752974" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
